#### *Ideas / Concepts on the Chopping Block*

- Throwaway ‘Minotaur’ epithets \- bullywag, minnow, bullhead, hornhead, bully-rock.   
- If we do flashbacks of the birth it would be good to use chloroform and a midwife, could be part of the story that the father / husband had the woman locked up in the sanitarium because of her "crazy" stories about the abandoned minotaur child, especially if he was a high society illusionist that hid his minotaur background much like his son was forced to do.  
- We can have those in Governmental power be called the “Mods.” As in modernists, or modernizers. The labour party could be adversarial and have a luddite subgroup. (See list of political parties)  
- [**Professional mourners**](https://metro.co.uk/2017/10/21/now-you-can-hire-professional-mourners-for-your-funeral-and-its-not-as-strange-as-you-might-think-7002481/)**:** “Professional mourners were also recorded in China in a New York Times article from 1877 that refers to ‘customs in the Orient’ for ‘hired mourners’. It reads: ‘The custom undoubtedly has its advantages. When an objectionable uncle dies, leaving his nephew a large fortune, the latter can save himself the strain of mourning his departed relative by merely hiring a few loud-voiced women to wail for a decent number of days. \[...\] ‘It is rather strange that, with our constitutional love of business and division of labour, we have not adopted this custom, or improved upon it by constructing ingenious mechanics mourners operated by steam.’”

#### *Notes taken from BOTTOM OF GAMESCRIPT DOCUMENT* 

- Failing a skill check triggers autosave to restrict save-scummers. The skill points are based on your actual actions, so the game doesn’t baby-sit you through making the character you want. Instead, you turn out based on your choices. There’s no skill-point selection. Even when you fail, a message shows, saying you’ll be better at lockpicking next time.  
- In the [East End Docklands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/19th-century_London), the "gin-problem" was never taken care of. Sort of like in the US there are gang injunctions and unfair, biased policing in certain cities, the 'billy-clubbers' (militarized govt. police) will go and raid the 'ghetto' areas, which are still under prohibition. A War on Drugs making the situation worse.  
- The Dockhounds are running the show… similar to the Kray twins (Ronnie and Reggie), who had the Firm protection and extortion ring for many years until the murder in the Blind Beggar in Whitechapel. Ronnie was still committed to Broadmoor hospital when he died. **For our Don of the Dockhounds, AKA Kingpin, he too will be a paranoid schizo, making him incredibly unpredictable and frightening.**   
- Sorris Square has a tunnel to the Underground locomotive-tunnels and the catacombs (maybe). Detail the statue and other interactables. The Chinese laundry is there, where Atticus meets Bixby’s wife in her Chinese laundry. He’s had his clothes ripped in a fight, or else needs a costume for one of the missions, and has to go there for tailoring.  
- Atticus’s gambling debt is extra motivation and backstory, but the story is primarily about him coming to terms with his upbringing and his mother and recovering from the consequences of his vices. He also wants the cadre of magical-born minotaurs in the world to accept him, once he discovers their community by way of a macguffin—the Magical Sceptre, which is not an actual item the player can ever possess.  
- A mission (for Clara?) in the London Underground, hinting at how labyrinthine, sunless and lonely the tunnels can be…’ The cult moves about in the tunnels.  
- The Masked Stranger pulls the team together for his own ends, as well as potential altruism as far as going up against ‘the Cult,’ maybe called ‘The Organ Grinders,’ who abduct orphans and prostitutes for their organ-harvesting and sacrificial ceremonies. The Stranger also leads of the Greatcoats, a secret society of magicians who never show their faces and work magic in the shadows, which in their opinion is the only way to work against the capitalist, secular regime amassing political power by the end of the prequels, beginning *Sovereign Syndicate* (the full game), where you end up facing the Cult Leader, who isn't evil so much as a victim of his upbringing and circumstance that perverted his world view.

Opening idea \- had it 8-30-20, 9pm \- Converted to another doc on 8-31  
A dark shape looms over you, swimming in and out of focus. If you didn’t hear a voice from the shadow above you, you couldn’t even be sure it was alive, or just a representation of the dark cloud of your week-long bender at rock bottom. Just a dark cloud covering the oily *gas-lanterns* flickering along the brick walls of this alleyway where you must have picked for a place to die. But the dark shape does have a voice. It speaks to you.  
	This ends up being a ‘mysterious figure,’ who convinces you to step into the opium den with him, after waking you up with a Victorian-era street-stimulant smelling-salt. You ask why he’s buying you a pillow and a pipe-sit, and he says he wants to help you.  
“If you really want to help me,” you say, “you’ll make that a triple dose and let me die the peaceful death of dreams.”   
He gives you a choice, to take the lethal dose, or to help him out, for which he offers to connect you with your mother. You’re hoping that she, too is/was a Minotaur, or at least your father was, and she can help you find him. Minotaurs are very rare.   
You can’t take him seriously, until he starts spouting off about the orphanage you came from and how he knows where she ended up.   
“How could you…?”  
“I’m very well-connected. Nothing gets by me, unless it’s for my own good.”  
Then if you take the death-dose, you end up at the Start Menu.  
If you take the Dark Stranger’s offer, you fall into an opium dream where the conversation reminds you of being a kid in the orphanage, and learning how to use your magic powers with the help of a kind nun who takes pity on you, so that you can hide your Minotaur nature and get bullied a lot less. Even so, you steal money from the lockbox and run away when you’re fifteen years old, which is fully grown and developed for a Minotaur, at least physically, although not as far as magical powers and training.   
You wake up having detoxed from the hangover via the opium, but there’s something funny about this opium come-down. You don’t have the urge to fill the void with another vice, like a few shots of gin. For some reason you seem to have a kind of resigned clarity you can’t remember having in a long time. There seems to be only the task ahead of you, to follow the mission orders from the Stranger in the Hooded Greatcoat.   
(There aren’t many Minotaurs who can do magic anymore, as the magical bloodlines have died off, for a reason which we will find out in the end of the story--it has to do with society not accepting them, and them needing to grow up in isolation to develop their abilities, much like our orphan did, and much like the one in the Labyrinth would have in the Greek Legend.)  
Because there aren’t many, the Stranger wants to groom you into a powerful Minotaur Mage, so as to unlock this hidden treasure of a magical sceptre with Midas-like powers of turning things into pure gold. He thinks the sceptre is buried in a Minotaur-access only vault inside an underground cult of Minotaur magicians, who have a hideout in the catacombs beneath Paris, and that they themselves don’t even know that the sceptre is there, for the person who once had it, hid it very well because they knew people would fight bloody, greedy wars to possess it. Too dangerous for anyone to own, so this Ancient Minotaur tried to hide it forever.   
Perhaps we find out that the Stranger himself is a Minotaur, but only half, or had one in his family bloodline, but anyway, no matter his race, the Stranger will test our Minotaur main character with at least one mission in the London Underground, hinting at how 'labyrinthine, sunless and lonely the tunnels can be…’ which is a little spot of foreshadowing, but not super obvious.  
\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_

Notes to consult for the orphanage flashback  
Netrem is a Clawdite, which makes him a changeling, or shapeshifter. Clawdites developed the ability to modify their skin color and body shape as a means to survival, after a spike in solar radiation beset the planet of Zolan, long ago while the species was evolving. Netrem was therefore blessed with a genetic resilience to disease. When his immune system encountered a virus or bacterial infection, it’d change as needed to fight it. Despite being a strong, healthy child, Netrem’s early years were no picnic. Due to his Clawdite nature, by age six the other children had taken to calling him “filthy beast,” refusing to sit near him, share food with him or invite him to play. Although the Tepani Sector wasn’t anti-alien per se, human businesses throughout the expanse provided their most lucrative opportunities to fellow Humans, and the wealth and opportunities trickled down through the noble houses and families, which consisted of solely human members.   
Netrem was physically bullied as well, often to the point of cuts and bruises that would come close to healing completely, only to be opened again by a troublesome orphan, who wasn’t provided an outlet for his disgruntled self-reflection of his own neglect. Seeing Netrem’s innocence being wrung out of him by these cruel, abandoned children broke nurse Paytela Bellbri’s heart.   
*\- Paytela’s Pursuit \-*   
Paytela was one of Netrem’s primary caregivers at the orphanage, and although she looked after others, she took a special liking to him, and helped him to perceive his changeling ability as a gift. It was only around Paytela that young Netrem was comfortable enough to fully experiment with his shapeshifting abilities. Later in life, it would take great concentration as well as loose, comfortable clothing for Netrem to change bodily form, but as a child, the weight of the world and his place in it had yet to reveal itself to Netrem. Without many friends at Light of the Vale, he spent his alone time in the safety of his favorite hiding spots. Once quite sure he was hidden, he would quiet his mind and focus deeply, the way children naturally can when they put their mind to it, and watch his fingers and toes turn into paws, fins or talons.  
By the time he was seven years old, Netrem began performing for Paytela in earnest, even hiding in her closet in the form of a tooka-cat and jumping out to scare her. Although Paytela started being able to predict when Netrem was in the closet, his playful leap towards her still sent her into jovial fits of laughter every time. Netrem as a striped tooka-cat was her favorite form he had mastered, since he reminded her of the loth-cat her family had kept around the house to control the population of loth-rats. Paytela’s family had emigrated from Lothal in the Outer Rim when she was seventeen.   
Although Paytela admired his abilities and positive outlook in the face of the other children’s prejudice, her pity for young Netrem outweighed such feelings. She knew once he emerged out of childhood and into adolescence, his ability to rise above the torment of the other children would falter, and she worried he would begin to lash out, as boys at such an age without loving role models are often known to do.  
Paytela spent many sleepless nights racking her brain for a wealthy family of nobles who might take Netrem in as a serving-boy. The most available choice was of course House Pelagia. Ladies and lords from the other noble families in the Tapani sector passed through Pelegar on business, but they’d be hard-pressed to stop at orphanage, much less adopt a young humanoid into their family. Besides, House Pelagia was the least xenophobic and most open-minded house, owing to a history of force-sensitive human members.  
It pained her dearly to imagine Netrem coming of age in the orphanage, growing older and older than the rest of the children, and eventually having more in common with the staff than the orphans under her care. As Paytela tended to the cuts and bruises Netrem would receive in his scuffles with the other boys, she couldn’t help but imagine him growing up to be a great soldier. Perhaps it was his stubborn resilience. As Netrem’s intelligence grew, Paytela noticed him coming up with clever ways to avoid the boys who tormented him. She hoped to come upon someone from House Pelagia with a tradition of raising up capable men into the military service. She could think of several military-minded noblemen who had served in the House Pelagia Airborne, a venerable affiliate and ally to the Tapani Sector Defense Force.  
*\- A Chance Encounter \-*   
One day Paytela was buying Jogan fruit at the market and ran into an old friend from primary school, Savamir Pellagra. Paytela immediately noticed Savamir had a governess doing the physical act of picking up, paying and putting the fruit in baskets for her. Savamir only made her selections and waited politely as her governess attended to her requests.   
As Paytela and Savamir were both between errands, they decided to stop for a caffa and catch up. Paytela noticed a wedding band as they chatted. Paytela congratulated her old friend and asked to whom she was married. Savamir told her his name was Tiersen, but didn’t reveal his last name. Paytela knew better than to press a noblewoman for information, especially being the commoner she was. To Paytela’s surprise and rekindled hope, Savamir told her it was a happy marriage, but that she and her husband had been having trouble conceiving.  
“To be perfectly honest,” Savamir said, “When you mentioned your work at the orphanage, I meant to inquire upon the process of adoption. Those poor, unfortunate children…”  
“Well,” Paytela said soberly. “It’s true that our resources have spread quite thin in the last few years, but we do our best to go above and beyond the call of duty to give the children a chance at adoption. That is the end goal for every last one of them.” Paytela bit her lip, carefully considering the best way to go on. “But the process is rather simple. We try to make it so.”  
They decided to meet again the following week, and after this meeting Paytela convinced Savamir to visit, assuming her husband did not object. Paytela’s heart swelled with anticipation for the day of Savamir’s visit. Paytela wondered if Savamir would feel a similar, raw pity for young Netrem who was now nearly nine years old and a wellspring of potential. By this point Netrem was far ahead of the other children his age, not only physically, but emotionally and intellectually as well.  
On the scheduled day of her visit, Savamir surprised Paytela by arriving along with her husband, Tiersen Pursal. Tiersen was a Baron, and Savamir a Baroness, although she’d been entirely tolerant to Paytela’s informal yet acceptable use of ‘my lady’ over the course of their re-connection. Paytela was taken aback, as she hadn’t prepared Netrem to meet his potential father as well. Paytela of course knew who Tiersen Pursal was. He ran a lucrative armony that supplied weapons and laser cannons to House Pelagia gunships. She smiled broadly and welcomed the couple, hoping she would have a chance to ask Savamir why she had been so careful not to reveal her husband’s identity, especially since it made her a Baroness.

###### **SORRIS SQUARE:**

**Sorris Square Subtext and Exposition Notes:** 

- We aren't sure if it's really a possessed statue, or if Poe is throwing his voice like a ventriloquist. We see the statue's portrait during this section of Dialog.

**Cut from the description of road-paving, etc:**

- The Big Smoke, otherwise known as London-town, is run by Crown and the upper crust of elite industrialists with economic sway,  
- Rooks (an alternate name for the Dockhounds/a rival gang) was taken out

**Older initial description in full:**

- At the Western edge of the East End, the mediaeval cobbles have all been flattened to dust. Even in Spitalfields and as far as Flower and Dean, the streets are smoothed over with a black bile of macadam. The work is done by the chaw-spitting navvies, mostly of humans and dwarf blood, eyes gleefully spiteful in the grips of a daily gin-craze. Fribbles and ninnies now glide upon pavement, in steam-powered, gilded cabriolets. And it makes no difference to the navvies that they might erase history—they’ll toil for any steady pay.   
  Yet preservation is alive in the Docklands. From Whitechapel to Cable, Parliamentary clauses have been grandfathered in, prohibiting the foundation of Lordships, whose sway will deliver the right building permits to the tar-tycoons in the rest of Her Majesty’s London. But here in the Docklands the Bosses are in charge, and the average popinjay avoids the area, for fear of ransom or robbery by the Dockhounds. Nobles with common sense hardly cross the River Lea, and anything East of Aldgate is a rare place for gentry. The Lordships and Ladyships who chance it in the East End must have an ear to the cobbles and old ways. They know the loopholes, willing to skim extra tin by a bribe to the right crime Bosses. Noble or not, anyone down in the Docklands on business is bound for a stop in Sorris Square—the apex of the informal economy.

###### **INFERNO:**

**Loading Text**  
A nondescript door at the end of the bar leads down the basement. The stairs are undecorated, with a mildewed mop askew in the corner, beside a copper bucket, as if to suggest the passage is only for utility access. But you know better, and a world of wager and chance awaits you at the bottom of the thinly carpeted steps. Adorning the mouldering stone walls, bare carbide lamps glare in smoky patterns, leading into the fiery pit of your vices.  
	After a knock at the door, a peephole slides open, and after checking his list of members, he opens the door. Inside it is filled with thick cheroot cigar smoke, and low-burning lanterns line the walls with embroidery-panels between the beams. The ceiling is low and stippled with brass, monogrammed with the crest of the Dockhounds, the local gang running the show here. Claret and gin flows freely. Chips clatter in and out of pewter bank trays, underscored by a murmur of velveteen voices. Now and then there’s a grumble or a chuckle of delight, depending on who’s up, and who’s down to the felt.  
	Men drift about in bespoke gambling coats, with low-brimmed hats covering eyes that might reveal their hands. Many have pulled back their lace cuffs and wrapped leather guards around them to protect their fine garments as they reach across the scuffed velvet for chips. Games of every kind in this Golden Hall—hidden well enough for even Lordships who brave the East End to risk their fortunes discreetly. Parlour-games from piquet to faro, from casino to ombre and quadrille, not to mention the betting book, where anything imaginable—from a bachelor’s choice of whom to marry, to the number of stray dogs crossing Cable street over an afternoon—can be bet upon.

- The Floorman (also the Don’s Lackey — known only in the parlour by a nametag showing — “Mister K.” AKA John Kirby) shows up, offering VIP treatment at Clara’s show, his motivation being that you don’t win more money off the House, b/c he sees your good string of luck.  
- The Player can decide whether this is due to an attraction to Clara, or trying to turn the luck towards himself at the expense of others. Crone/Atticus decide that it’s better to play it cool and not call Clara out. The Crone gives advice as always, while Atticus is influenced by a subconscious attraction to Clara.  
- Clara takes a liking to you more so than George or Sydney; but Persuasion is still needed. She becomes (ostensibly) a good luck charm, but whether she was a Cooler or not, the Baccarat players have already won enough beforehand to walk away happily.   
    
  **CHESTER MARTIN REMOVED**  
- SPR. A stout fellow with the look of a seaman is blowing on the dice, getting ready to roll, but when I sit down, he cuts his eyes sharply in my direction.  
- (Hearty Gambler) TIM. Another player, ay? I liked the table as it was.  
- (Kind Gambler) CHE. Aww, don’t be like that. This Parlour is open to all and besides, what’s the use of an empty chair? Now then, my name is Chester Martin. I work as a chimney sweep all through the East End, then I dump most of my wages into this money pit. Anyway, there’s no sense in griping. I can stop when I want to.   
- TIM. He just doesn’t want to.  
- CHE. Maybe that’s fair enough. Say now, what’s the new player’s name?  
- SPR. Lad’s a {sweep} alright. Fellow could use a wash. Anyroad, no point lying. The staff know you here.  
- WIT. Martin has oily black streaks behind his ears and on his neck. Must’ve been in a rush. Anyway, there’s no point in giving a false name—the croupiers and pit bosses all know you here.   
- PC. Name’s Atticus Daley. Pleasure to meet you. And your friend here?  
- TIM. If Chester is willing to get acquainted, so am I. Name’s Timothy Agarwal, but Timothy is fine. Now then, let’s stopper the chitchat and cast.   
- CHE. If only you knew when to stopper the whisky bottle.  
- TIM. There’s no fault to be found there—I married an Irish lass, so maybe her habits rubbed off on me. Anyway, I function much better with a little fire in my belly.  
- CHE. Let’s hope the dice don’t disagree.  
- (cont’d)  
- HAZ. {Caster}? What’ll it be?  
- TIM. I’ll take seven.  
- HAZ. Caster has seven, place your special bets. Ready?  
- SR. The croupier wears a brown vest with shiny brass buttons. His skin is the shade of a tallow candle, like a wax figure. Surely he’s been in this basement far too long.  
- SPR. The croupier obsessively licks his fingers before collecting chips from the players and straightening the stacks, sliding them to their destinations within the coloured squares on the felted table.

- SR. Timothy wears a tailored, split-tailed, brushed velvet waistcoat, the brass buttons long since green with oxidisation. A sash-loop dangles free of its piping, and the paisley lapels are frayed to the innermost fibres. Surely it’s secondhand, only purchased so as to gain entrance.   
- CHE. Hurry now, throw in while the dice are hot\!

**Wooden Bridge Animation / Trigger Instructions —**   
If: Perception — Smell — Success: Display the dotted line of the Captain’s patrol-path — from the lower level up to the door to the Control room, across the Wooden Bridge, and back down. Camera zoom-out if possible. (Wooden Bridge)  
IF: Perception failure, and decision to still run across the Wooden Bridge, Cue Animation of Atticus ‘winding up’ to run across, then hastening across the planks. Fade to Black. Fade back to Sewer, where the bridge is now half-broken and impassable. (Wooden Bridge)  
Animation of Pumphouse Captain hustling over to confront Atticus for breaking the bridge. (Wooden Bridge)  
IF: success, strong sections of planks are illuminated one-by-one, with a ‘don’t-click’ symbol on the weaker areas. Player clicks them one by one, and each triggers as a tiptoeing animation for Atticus. Player can now cross the bridge at will, but still clicks the planks one by one. (Wooden Bridge)  
IF: decision is made to ‘chance it,’ Display Animation of Atticus walking across. At the halfway point, Sound Cue — wood cracking. Fade to Black, trigger Death Screen. (Wooden Bridge)

*Random idea(s):* 

- Mr. Welcome — a nickname for Atticus, b/c he’s ‘Welcome anywhere.’ It’s from when he used to pay his debts, but now it’s used ironically, and the Ladsman can reveal this, now that he sees his face and recognizes him. Atticus doesn’t remember at first, and the Player can choose whether this is due to gin-bathing, or honest forgetfulness (+1 Composure)  
- *By completing the Interrogate McGrady Quest, the Ladsman is persuaded to reveal the details of the organ-shopping / snatching for Mr. Cline, but if pressed on this point, he will lash out, and only reveal details if Atticus promises to spare his life. Player chooses to keep that promise or not.*  
- *Dialogue with Atticus and Ladsman where they reminisce about growing up as pickpockets*

  A \- Minotaur wins a majority of Skill Checks. Ladsman switches from Combat Standard to Wounded Idle to Wounded Prone as Vigour is depleted, to the point that the Ladsman is blubbering for mercy, gasping like a landed fish by blows from the Cane-sword, both blade and bludgeoning from the hilt.   
  B \- Ladsman is wounded enough so that Cutpurse can finish the job with a stiletto to the Ladsman’s throat from behind, but she only does so if the Minotaur is low enough in Vigour (Wounded idle).  
  C \- Ladsman wins a majority of Skill Checks, resulting in Player Choice to either flee, in which case the Cutpurse flees and the Ladsman follows her, meaning SavedCutpurse is still false.

###### **THE BATHHOUSE:**

...Wit: Maybe they like positions from which they can proselytise. 

...Old Crone: The Bathhouse walls are lined with bamboo, and a huge Chinese lantern hangs in place of a chandelier. A steaming square tub sits in the centre of the floor, tiled with ambergris marble. Pots of incense burn down to yellow coals, wafting steam into a dream-like ethos. Wood panels on the back wall are carved with bucolic landscapes from the Far East; misty clouds in high mountains. One of the wood panels is cracked open slightly, and a red light slivers through. The hidden entrance to the opium den.

Opening \-   
…Old Crone: Despite the lingering body-aches and nausea, you do feel much better don’t you? Just the thought of that sweet opium release is enough to lift your spirits.  
*As close as I’ll ever be…* I’ve never been happy… but I’ve gotten close in this place.  
Journal Entry \- My favourite opium den could it be coincidence that the stranger has led me here?

Revamped Opening \-   
Alternate lines \- And remember when you were happy. No way to erase it. / And remember that time you said you were happy. It never has to fade.

Changing Area \-   
Concentrate now, Atticus, you can do this.  
Never seen that bouncer at the back bar before. Better look Human, in case he gets his knickers in a twist **when he sees a Minotaur.**  
Holding this form takes all my concentration, best save my wits for defending myself if it comes to that.  
Alt \- Sight from the fire, hearing from ether, smell from the air and taste from the water... Focus your senses and touch down to the earth in another form.

Mahogany Bar \-   
…A brass-linteled, mahogany bar sits before the back wall, with a Centaur bouncer behind it, wearing a drowsy look and resting his chin in his hands. Candles gutter on the scrub-top bar, casting eerie shadows on his weary face. Judging by the cloying scent of mange, his burly lower-half must be in poor shape as well. You can smell the equine muck-sweat even through the haze of incense.  
Why did it have to be a Centaur?  
Centaurs are a detestable bunch, most of them at least. They always seem to get a rush from a power trip; any position from which they can proselytise. Except for the owner of the Red Lotus, Bixby Browncoat. Mr. Browncoat is oft-times waiting at the bar with a casual smile, but not tonight.  
1 \- Maybe if I wait around long enough Bixby will show up?  
2 \- Better to appear human in situations like these. No need to cause a scene and I'm in no mood to fight.  
3 \- Fortune favours the bold; better get on with it.

Bouncer \-   
…Askew on the Centaur’s head is a bowler hat, banded with imitation-silk. He straightens up and leers at you with beady, black eyes, misshapen chin jutting out below his jangle of buck-teeth. Beneath a crimson vest, his bare chest is stricken with advanced psoriasis. The scaly rash covers his pock-marked cheeks as well.  
The smelly Centaur glares directly at you without a word. Before you can break in, the stranger steps forward, foreseeing the impending row.  
Hail and well met. Fine spot of the weather, eh?  
Somefin’ the matter? the Centaur asks, plainly addressing you, not the stranger.  
…The stranger tries to cut in but the damage is done. ‘Heifer’ is one of the worst slurs for a Minotaur.  
…I don’t think it’s the incense I’m smelling. I think it’s the horse-shit spilling from your fat, manky mouth. So you better shut it before it gets swelled shut.  
…You brandish your sword stick **with a white-knuckle grasp on the handle**. / You prepare to draw your blade with a white-knuckle grasp…  
…That’ll get you inside… As for the sirloin… Policy is policy.  
…I’d like a word with the owner, please. We happen to be on a  
first-name basis.  
…The Centaur whinnies indecisively. You slap an impatient palm on  
 the bartop.

…Got nothing to do with what I has to say. It’s just we has a policy ‘gainst filthy, ruddy cow-pies. Boss ain’t havin’ no more fightin’ in the den. Your lot’s always bringin’ it around. Bulls in a China shop… Not good for business.

…Well, perhaps so. Needless to say, I haven't a slim notion of why I should delay you any further\! Go right ahead, then. And sorry for the wait.

…ALT. Stricken with psoriasis, the scaly rash reddens his chest and pock-marked cheeks.

…I slap a hand on the bartop, and the Centaur flares his nostrils in contempt, sweeping his waistcoat to reveal a long dagger.  
…Who does this ruffian think he is? Whatever my next move, I'd better be swift about it.

Bixby \-   
…Seemingly on cue the wood panel behind the bar swings open, and out trots Bixby Browncoat. No doubt, come to see what all the fuss is about.  
…Seemingly on cue, the wood panel behind the bar swings open, and to the stranger's relief, it’s Bixby. No doubt to come see what all the noise is about.  
…Bixby Browncoat, the owner proprietor of the Red Lotus appears. He has a distinguished, long-faced countenance, sporting a gold pocket watch and a lavender-tinted pince-nez with octagonal frames, settled low on his aquiline nose. Despite his refined style and careful preening, the turbulence of a life lived in the margins shows on his face, with a river-delta of wrinkles. He peers over his pince-nez with his deep-set eyes, the same sienna-brown as his coat of fur.

###### **OPIUM DEN:**

- **​​Automaton \-**   
  A clattering of gears grabs your attention. Spinning round, you nearly pitch over, having to stumble your cloven feet out of the way of a swerving automaton underfoot.   
  The mechanised creature is huffing along by way of an Arsenal Heartdrum steam-boiler. His chassis is a perfect sphere, with ball-jointed legs that broaden into conical, pressure-pad feet. His brass-capped head spins like a lighthouse lamp.  
  Sorry, didn’t see you there\!  
  What the—  
  The automaton is clicking and whirring along past you, coming to rest at the booth beside yours, where a plump, ginger-bearded dwarf is hunched over the table. He must be the rude robot’s master.  
  (GLOSSARY) \-  A design firm for advanced machinery

  The sunken floor-pit is dotted with satin pillows, each costing only a ha’penny. It’s a busy night. About half the pillows are taken. Those on the main floor are withered and weak-looking, all of them men. Sallow-cheeked blokes with beards down to their bellies and smoke-stained moustaches. They look so comatose, they might not be able to tell you their own name.  
  The main floor is usually all you can afford. As Bixby said, you’re quite welcome here, even in Minotaur form. Even so, a tuppence will only get you a half-bowl and a spot on the floor. With the shylocks always at your heels, tracking your every move in the East End, the most you can ever save up is a few pence.

  Old Crone: You’ve had it. You can’t exist in this mess of a life you’ve made. Bixby brings over a large lacquered bowl, usually reserved for parties of four or five.   Old Crone: Testing the texture with a ceramic serving spoon, you scoop out a heaping pile of the crumbly concentrate, rich and pale tan like foamy espresso. The aroma is intoxicating, making your skin crawl with yearning. 

  Old Crone: You light up, inhaling the acrid smoke deeply. The longer you hold your breath, the more that your lungs burn, crying out for oxygen. By the time you breathe out again, the red walls are misty and light seems like a lie. Darkness envelops your body and mind, as the grim angel of death appears in your vision. A hooded figure, offering a pale white hand from its cloak. A hand which you take as it pulls you to your feet. Weightless. Lacking in feeling and emotion. This is the end; the glory omniscient

  (Atticus dies. A “Game Over” screen appears, along with the preceding text ↑)

  Other, older cuts \- 

- Attorneys and prosecutors, prison wardens, billy-clubbers and Orthodox mercenaries… Centaurs fall into law-enforcement with ease. He’s the only Centaur you’ve met who tolerates all manner of creatures, including Minotaurs.

- (We took out the smoke-bomb illusion transition.)

  ...The stranger is still at your heels like a shadow, and the both of you follow Bixby inside, where the Red Lotus is draped in a haze of pale smoke. The opium-smell is like overdone biscuits, and only dim shapes emerge in the tendrils. The red-papered walls are etched in calligraphy, lit up by sconces laden with lanterns. Women in kimonos are floating about, carrying trays of tea and opiums. Pipes light up in the dark like cinders. 

  Priority Members avoid the central pit, opting for discretion within the private booths. Dark eyes bore down from behind wooden screens, protecting their fragile reputations. The time here is twisted in a strange uncertainty, where a string of days can pass in the course of one night. With enough capital you could dream your life away. 

  ...The walls themselves are covered with needlepoint wallpaper, a fine silk embroidery hand-painted with cherry-blossom sprays. Between patches of wallpaper is the crumbling brick of the old foundation, drilled with iron sconces and prickets for grease lamps. Low-burning lanterns hang from the ceiling on thin wires obscured by the smoke so they appear to be floating. Wrapped in red glass, they cast a rosy glow about the room. Red painted canvases hang on the walls, with delicate calligraphy of Chinese characters: symbols of luck, friendship, and wealth among others. 

  Ghostly women in kimonos move about, opening red-lacquered cabinets for tea and opium. They carry trays with china-handled teapots and repeating-matches, flitting down mostly to the main floor, where the men are too strung-out to light their own pipes. In this case, the staff holds the pipe to the patrons’ lips. Shadowy figures peer out from the private booths, seemingly more in control of their blue-smoke dreamscapes. They’re well-dressed and hidden by the latticed cherrywood screens, as if they had reputations to ruin if seen here. 

  ...Mahogany bunk beds run along the walls, their frames carved with Chinese characters—luck, friendship, wealth, and so on. Between them are the private booths and cushy benches. Red-velvet brocade curtains hang from the crossbeams, creating privacy for those who can afford it. The beds and deluxe seating roundabout the room in a horseshoe shape, circling the largest bit of territory—the pit. 


  …They won’t receive tea with their simple ivory pipes. The white-jade pipes with bands of shagreen; those are reserved for the flash clientele. When the men on the main floor run out of money, they’re given some water to cope with their cotton-mouth, then promptly led through the back door to the street. They might only be gone for a few hours, however long it takes to beggar some more pence. 

  ...As for yourself, the main floor is usually all you can afford. \[...\] But tonight you’re getting special treatment. Bixby must feel bad for his cousin accosting you. Not to mention the stranger’s pocketbook— as fat as a Christmas goose. Which begs the question: Why take an interest in a penniless sot like you? You still can’t start trusting the person behind the mask. But you have to admit, you’d rather be in a cosy private booth in your favourite opium den, than the vomit soaked alleyway-deathbed you came from.

  The dwarf has a warm and amiable look, with the sort of lucid blue eyes you can’t stay angry at. His gaze is so sharp and clearly intelligent, that you find yourself intrigued, as opposed to annoyed. Below his crystal-blue eyes is a broad nose and a red moustache which is so full, you expect it may crawl off his face and build a cocoon. His beard is as red as a skinned rabbit, and braided and brass-ringed in the common style. By reflex, you finger the brass ring in your own goatee. It’s stringy and coarse compared to the dwarf’s beard, which spilled out in red waves on the table. A calabash tobacco pipe waggles from his mouth, and whenever he chuckles, the embers dance and glow. The dwarf has a mechanised-arm for his left, and although you cannot see below the table, you get the impression he has quite a few more  augmentations. 

  Protruding from behind his head is an induction spark-coil, attached to a backpack the dwarf is either wearing, or has welded to his back-plate armour. Although the coil is not currently twisting with lightning-waves, incandescent bulbs burn along the iron frame, so the dwarf must have energy saved up in the dry-cells of his power-pack. Black steam burps out from a small boiler-top, jutting out from the side at a right angle.

  Taking in the dwarf’s mechanical modifications, you decide to play it off like nothing happened. “Some kind of inventor, are you? Designed that rickety thing?”

  “Right you are. The name’s Theodore. Theodore Redgrave. But most people just call me Teddy. This little bucket of brass here is Otto. Doesn’t care much for other people, but that’s in his programming. Can’t blame him, really. I’m the one who can’t build a better action-grid. Those Babbage machines have all the best patents. Need me a lassie who can work me a new algorithm. Then I’ll get ahead of those Mods and start my own firm. Anyway, I’m sorry if he got in your way. Can I get you lads a cuppa tea to set things right?”

  “We’ve got the tea coming already, thanks,” the stranger says curtly.

  You open your mouth to say something, but suddenly, your tongue feels too large for your mouth. You glance quickly at the stranger, who’s muttering under his breath, and you realise he’s cursed you again. He doesn’t want you to talk to Teddy Redgrave for some reason. And if you ever want your tongue to return to normal size, you figure it’s best to go along with what the stranger wants. You stare wide-eyed at the dwarf in the next booth, who stares back for a moment with a quizzical look. He was expecting you to say something, but eventually he shrugs and turns away.

  “Alright then,” Teddy says. “I'll let you get on with it.”

He gives you both a wink and small nod, then steps away. “Take all the time you need. Remember, Atticus, you should feel at home here.”

**Death and dream dose screens**  
ALT: You cannot hold on to this mess of life you’ve made. When the order arrives, the server gives the stranger a worried glance, but the stranger waves him off with a look that assumes full responsibility for the deadly amount of opium on the table. The crumbly concentrate is the colour of espresso, and the smell makes your skin crawl with yearning. Lighting up, inhaling to the bottom of your breath, you hold in the smoke while your lungs cry for oxygen. If you ever exhale, you don’t feel it happen, but the red walls are misty and light seems to be telling lies. Darkness envelops your body and mind, as the angel of death appears in a wisp of smoke. The hooded figure offers a pale hand, pulling your soul from the weight of your body. This is the end, the Glory Omniscient.

###### **ORPHANAGE (FLASHBACKS):**

You take the stranger’s offer, eager to lose touch with harsh reality. You fall into an opium dream, where the stranger’s recent questions about your past remind you of growing up at the Sacred Heart Orphanage.   
Gauzy light streaks in through a window. Lying in a musty dormitory bed, you wake to the sight of a nurse sitting beside you. She has a kind smile and mousy brown hair. This is Heloise Clements, the only nun at the orphanage who ever took pity on you.  
As you come back to consciousness, Heloise presents a fresh bandage for your head, tending to one of the many wounds you sustained in the dooryard scuffles with the bellicose children at the Sacred Heart. If they weren’t hurling stones or insults, they were ignoring you completely. The pain of this unjustified state of affairs is reflected in her eyes, welling with tears of comprehension, as her hands wrap the bandage around the wound.  
**SPLASHSCREEN SUPERIMPOSE \- Sacred Heart Orphanage: Twenty-Five Years Ago**   
\[...\]  
Another gauzy memory, all floating particles of uncorporeal light… Children are gathered in the dooryard, encircling you, shouting something at you. The dooryard is all wild grass and the high-summer air is so close that it’s cruel. And it hurts to remember… They’re demanding something… that’s it… they want you to perform your Illusion.  
The Orphanage was always presided over by the local Parish. A few members of the House of Lords and their philanthropic wives had made donations, but for the most part the Church provided the Sisters with barely enough provisions to go around. There were no second helpings, unless stolen from another plate. The hunger in the boys’ bellies spilled into their social hierarchy; a fountain of bilious fear turned to anger.   
Some of the older orphans went out in the early mornings to work at the Shipyards, or seek out odd jobs in the streets. One of them, Leo, had even built his own bicycle-cabriolet, and spent his days shuttling day-wagers around the city. Leo was as close as you ever got to a friend here. But he’s timid and gangly, and in no position to defend you from the boy leading the chant—James Marker. You will have to face Jimmy on your own.  
\[...\]  
The place seemed colder and harsher by the day.  
\[...\]  
Characters and Interactables: Leo Giacometti (a dwarf), James “Jimmy” Marker, Father Franco, The Old Ice Machine, The Swing Set, The Seesaw  
\[...\]  
Rain pounds the windows and lightning flashes. All the way up the stairs and you’re crouching at the office door, with the hand-torch and the bump keys you stole from the custodian closet, quietly trying each key in the office door, unless the delightful clicking sound is heard.   
It’s a shame to have betrayed the haggard Cyclops custodian, who is the only non-Human soul at the Sacred Heart. But you’ve reached the point of no return, and burying your guilt, you slip inside the office, where the money you need for escape might await you.  
\[...\]  
PC.WIT. I’ve gotta take a slash. Go back to sleep, unless you want to watch?  
SNY. Ugh, no thank you. You are a foul one. (End)  
\[...\]  
On the eve of your thirteenth birthday, you lie awake going over your plan, and when you’re sure that the last night-owl is asleep, you creep from the dormitory bedroom on bare hooves, trying your best to muffle the sound of your hoofsteps. \[...\] An (Intuition Check) compels Young Atticus to keep searching the office… Atticus Daley: I’ve already lost their trust by breaking in… So what else can I find? The Player stumbles over a file cabinet stuffed with loose sheafs of printed records on parchment. Your name is among them, and just as you slide your file out, you hear footsteps coming down the hallway. There’s no time to read over your records, so you quickly hide the Lockbox inside your patched overcoat. \[...\] There’s enough money in the lockbox to last you a few months on your own—enough time to get far, far away from the Sacred Heart. \[...\] Tumbling out the window and into a hedgerow, you slip away unnoticed from the Orphanage, ready to carve out a life of your own. Yet twenty-five years later, you’re a full-grown Minotaur, still scrappy and homeless. If there’s any Virtues you have left, it’s your gnawing search for belonging and a passion for the ways of Magic and Illusions.  
\[...\]  
INS: Oh yes, the Royals will avoid scandal at all costs.

ORPHANAGE \- DORM \- NIGHT WITHIN DREAM \#1 — That Cyclops is the only other non-Human soul at Sacred Heart, treated like filth by reason of blood. But there’s no turning back now. Burying your guilt, you gather your determination.  
\[...\]  
The outlash against your Minotaur blood is incomprehensible to your developing mind, and despite the best efforts of the Sisters, you’ve begun stealing for sport—rosaries from church, gimcrack shivs from the older orphans, and bread from the kitchen.

Old Loading Screen (EXT)  
The cobblestones glisten with dew as you breathe deep of the brisk morning air. Your mood rising with the sun, you’re beginning to understand the merits of getting up early. You turn down the Sorris Square backstreet leading to the orphanage. The sagging facade is weathered and stripped, shuttered by pine flats where the windows were broken—it’s even shabbier now than when you ran away.  
Pain and regret twist your insides at the sight. You wish you had never stolen from the Sisters, but there’s no way to reverse your transgression, only make good on it if you can. You press on through the morning mist, which seems to conceal vaporous faces from your past—Heloise, Matilda, even the ruthless bullies of your childhood. At last you step free of the clinging mist and into the cobbled forecourt, where a {bluebander} stands guard at a barricade, observing your approach with a smug grin. You nod politely, and he summons his best sneer, as if you were something to scrape from the bottom of his boot.

Without the bobbies watching over affairs, some kind of evil Magic like a dark cloud seems to have settled in. A dark energy has swept in when the coppers took their leave.  
  A cold shiver runs down your spine, surveying the chipped and yellowed wall-tiles, in silent testimony to the horrors that have transpired over so many years. The wood floors have long since stopped being polished, and the smell of pine is missing now, replaced with a heavy musk of decay within each particle of air.

There’s a murmur of voices overhead, which can only be the children committed to the grim uncertainty here. Perhaps in the washroom, there’s a dripping pipe that echoes along the corridor attached to the foyer.

- ...Also inside is a Journal. Picking up this item opens the Journal Page, where **the Player is prompted to write down the events of that day**. They may refuse to, clicking ‘Not now.’ If choosing to write, all they have to do is type in two sentences, which show up on the parchment as legible, cursive letters. (They could write nonsense, but I hope some players will actually reflect on the events of the game, and could make for share-worthy content for the game-community.) After at least ten words and two periods have been inputted, a text box appears which says, ‘That’s all for now.’ Player can keep writing, but will eventually click the box to move on. Everytime the Player journals the events of the day, it will add a point to Intellect, Focus, and Persuasion (unbeknownst to the Player). Also, after the first time journaling, they unlock an option to read the previous journal entries (Player can write their own entries).

- **Angus Malone (Original)**  
  Angus Malone has a shiny bald head and rusty-blond Donegal beard. His arms are wallpapered with blue and black tattoos. He’s still having a task with cleaning the glasses, so he only offers an indistinct grumble when you approach. Based on your frequent patronage, the two of you are well-acquainted. Malone drinks like a sailor, and yet you’ve never heard him slurring his words or seen his hands shake—his tolerance is that high. Strongly proud of his Scottish kinship, he’s always blaming the Irish for the most belligerent of hijinks, claiming the Scottish hold their liquor far better. Angus Malone has a penchant for stories and gossip, so the only way he will serve you during his prep-time is to butter him up.

- **Original Load Screen (Night 1 \- After Gambling)**  
  After your lucky night, your head is full of steam and the bar is full of smoke, dancing and music. There’s still that clawing feeling that you could lose it all, but somehow you know you won't, because you don’t want to. And at least for now, while the vigour is high, the stage lights are low, and the anticipation of the Burlesque program is thick in the air, there’s nothing you’d rather do but toss back another glass of gin, ideally some variety in the latest taste—Beefeater, even—as money is no object, and relish in your good luck.  
  The ceiling is awash in the colourful lights of a hyper-sequenced magic lantern show being shuffled in rainbow-hued shadowplay. A red-velvet curtain is drawn across the stage, but a full band of ragtime instruments can be heard behind it, tuning up and ready to accompany the illustrious singer of the evening, whose name is in marquis lights above the stage — Clara Reed. You recognize the name, having been to the Palladium many times, but because of the bewildering clouds of gin and laudanum burdening your memory, you cannot recall her face, nor the tenor of her voice. It must be another sprig of luck—catching the show just as you came up from the Parlor. Excitement runs through your veins like electricity.

  - Old Crone: You’re right, I apologise. I shouldn’t stick around just to send you spiralling. But at the same time, you don’t seem to have a choice.  
  - Mr Betteredge: Stop that mumbling at once\! You’ll do what I ask, and then we’ll confer, and if anything goes awry, you won’t survive our next meeting.

###### **MANOR:**

- **\[MOVED FROM NIGHT TO DAY\]** There’s a changing of the guard at the wheelhouse past midnight, so if there’s any time to stick, that’s it.  
- Yes, this is the time to strike, when the seventeen fireplaces have all been banked, and the heirs have been tucked in, the Hellhounds penned to your smaller enclosure so as not to tussle with stray beasts from the bordering forest, when the Baron has had his nightcap and double-bowl of imported Virginia hash, and Baroness Claudia Fullivole has had her hair washed and rolled into curlers by her handmaidens, and her feet rubbed and oiled, a water-bottle folded into her bedclothes in the magisterial four-poster—when the fairytale of it all lies laden the dust of pleasant dreams—that is when you move.

A crime of passion, but also an end to what would have been the Dorrison-Dufrain bloodline.

#### *Notes Outtakes*

- Because there aren’t many, the Stranger wants to groom you into a powerful Minotaur Mage, so as to unlock this hidden treasure of a magical sceptre with Midas-like powers of turning things into pure gold. He thinks the sceptre is buried in a Minotaur-access only vault inside an underground cult of Minotaur magicians, who have a hideout in the catacombs beneath Paris, and that they themselves don’t even know that the sceptre is there, for the famous magician who had it, hid it very well because he knew people would fight bloody, greedy wars to possess it—too dangerous for anyone to own, so this Ancient Minotaur tried to hide it forever.

#### *Sisters in Spirit — First Draft and following Iterations*

###### **VELVET ROSE:** 

- This Easy Task (sneaking back through the Bedroom) has a high chance of succeeding, and even the failure results end with the Derringer back in Clara’s hands, so that the Player feels accomplished right away. The Player hits the streets again, but on her way back to her room, the Royal Suite at the Bell Jar Hotel

###### **Hints for Clara**

- Zora's Diary: The final clue that's quite difficult to come by, needs to be stolen from her apartment with a set of high skill checks, or else procured by another NPC, maybe Lefty Broan or Molly or a courtesan who Clara persuades to steal it from Zora. Written in Bruslavian, Clara needs either Nina or Ivana to translate it for her (both speak Bruslavian), and the Diary details every murder she committed, as well as intentions to frame Sykes the Werewolf. This 'nail in the coffin' clue is enough to convict Zora AND prove Sykes is innocent.

###### **Early Writing Exercise for Clara**

- Note to self: Try to write Clara’s story as it pertains to her original alignment to motivate herself to the main mission of hunting down the Courtesan Killer herself — in her own hands.  
- ESTABLISHING \- character daily or nightly routine if taking place at night   
- Clara in the mirror going to meet A man,   
  A contact by word of mouth, clientele potentially only if the bill fits the sale.  
  Clara Heyward didn't bend over backwards for just any cove with some scratch tin and a capital trust staked behind it.  
  They were the sort of popinjays to purchase a Lordship for just under their weight in gold, more so for the thrill of shedding coin than for the rush of a bargain. And for this man, such a mountain of Guineas would still not have nicked at the wealth of his prior generations, who had long passed and passed their inheritance. The oldest members of the Crown’s Royal family, The burgeoning plunder of war and allocation   
  Of trade privileges and redistribution of wealth  
  Within the confines of the upper class blue-book  
  Of names and addresses where another well heeled citizen of her majesty’s kingdom might rest their heavy heads and expect eggs and kippers in the morning, as well as their last night’s bespoke peacoats and silken ruffles vests with double-breasted waistcoats, laundered and fresh in the morning, hanging quite literally and possessing the lingering scent of rose blossoms in the spring, sprinkled across a field of wildflowers in season.  
  The Detective Character: (Based on Ebenezer Fraser in D.E.) **This ‘detective’ is now Yves, the Private Eye**

### **Worldbuilding \-** 

### London itself suffers from an imbalance in Humours 

Big idea to nest long lore explanations in Bookcases in our world

#### [*North America in Our World*](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1P3jS4YxHgSD_2ir3vZCQEsnP7pfNKv6icW-E9h0si44/edit?usp=sharing)

**Scott’s Comments on Sheila’s doc (North America in Our World)**

- Did things go differently here because of magic and myth?  
- How has steam technology affected the relationship between colonisers and indigenous states?  
- I'm particularly fascinated by the question of what Aztec and Mayan culture would look like in the 1800s. Would their way of life change to accommodate European society (as Japan did), or would they stay true to their old ways?  
- As above, it would also be interesting to see how Europe's culture might be influenced by the export of art, artefacts, traditions, etc. from Mayan/Aztec cities  
- How would someone from those cultures adapt to life in the old world?

#### *Roma / Romani*

- From Sheila: Need to be cautious about using the word gypsy outright. We could also shift the history of our specific setting in such a way that that term never came about. Perhaps the Romani people just weren't misnamed as such by Europeans during the 16th century in our world and/or adopted a different moniker. Hard to say what's most sensible. Obvi.  
- Could find serendipitous ways to refer to Romani characters that just don't make use of the slur unless it's a sequence where it's being called out the the one from Scott above. Simply use their name, or other characteristics (A woman from Brisbane with dark hair, or what have you). It certainly might be a bit of thought, but at the end of the day, it's not really our story to personally tell, and likely worth the effort  
- Patrin \- a handful of leaves or grass thrown down at intervals by Romany people to indicate their course  
- Romani witchcraft \- [link to full text of book](https://www.gutenberg.org/files/58465/58465-h/58465-h.htm)  
- The Black Madonna, honoured by [annual festival in Saintes-Maries](https://www.theguardian.com/travel/2011/mar/26/saintes-maires-gypsy-festival-camargue)

#### *Black Dogs / Hellhounds*

- Gwyllgi (either gwyllt "wild" or gwyll "twilight" \+ ci "dog") \- mythical black dog from Wales that appears as an English mastiff with baleful breath and blazing red eyes. Baleful meaning deadly/noxious. Mastiffs are distinguished by enormous size, massive head, short coat in a limited range of colours, and always displaying a black mask  
- In English folklore, [Black Shuck](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Shuck), Old Shuck, Old Shock or simply Shuck is the name given to a ghostly black dog which is said to roam the coastline and countryside of East Anglia, one of many such black dogs recorded in folklore across the British Isles.

#### 

#### *Cyclopes*

- From at least the fifth century BC, cyclopes have been associated with the island of Sicily and the volcanic Aeolian Islands. Humans being the dominant race, they gave our cyclopes this ‘homeland’ sanctuary as recompense for all the land that had been forcibly removed from in the past in order to establish human-dominated cities with human-dominated political systems that rewarded humans above minority races. But, nobody really wanted to settle or develop or harvest resources on the Aeolian Islands anyway, so human leaders who made the deal didn’t feel like it was a raw one for them, and they got to save face against progressive public scrutiny. By the time Atticus wakes up in the ally, the Aeolian Islands are developed and fitted out with luxury homes, hotels, religious temples, museums, and the wealthy elite cyclopes all either own property there or dream of purchasing it in the future.  
- Akin to the Mythology, our cyclopes were involved in blacksmithing, talented metalworkers by nature, resistant the heat and arduous conditions, able to maintain focus on the red-hot molten point of a blade, without the need for depth of field specific to detailed work that dwarves and even humans had a better knack for.   
- Because of genetic complications by breeding cyclopes with one another, their numbers became scarce, and the single eye being recessive meant that hybrids would often pass for another ethnicity, which gave them more privileges, leaving the single eyed cyclopes to be often-labelled as ‘monsters.’

#### 

#### *Lycans / Werewolves*

#### 

- The socially acceptable/civilised thing is to commit oneself each month, but some people avoid doing it for fear of being discriminated against—leading to werewolf hunters often called to deal with them outside containment (especially wealthy ones who might otherwise conceal their status). Containment areas are lawless zones for one day a month, poorly managed and profit motivated. You can have illegal fights and gambling, and people punished by crimes or vendettas by being thrown inside, and also falsely reported as werewolves for political reasons—committed against their will without evidence. Teddy Redgrave is a for-hire trophy monster-hunter, who’s hunted minotaurs before, so he can smell Atticus.  
- In England at least, those with Lycanthropy are required to register, which affects their employment opportunities, access to medical care and services, etc. Collection of the "lycans'' or some other slang could begin a few days before the full moon. They all get rounded up if they don't submit themselves voluntarily. So when Atticus checks the gate, it says, "With just a few days until the next full moon the containment zone is already starting to fill up with the more willing and civil among the **afflicted(*wc*)**, but there's always an element of risk when dealing with their kind." or something to that effect.   
- In Bruslavia (made up country in the Balkans), a vast-majority werewolf nation, the virus is known as Vukašin (meaning son of wolf)  
- A couple days later, Teddy escorts Atticus to an abandoned warehouse in the containment zone for the bare knuckle boxing match, knowing that he's a minotaur. The fight then occurs on the full moon with the werewolf and minotaur in natural form. If Atticus wants to bet on himself (or against himself) he has to use his illusion form as they won't let fighters bet on themselves.  
- Only humans are affected by the virus. Minotaurs, centaur, and dwarves were made of different blends of magical elements before they manifested into earthly bodies. The magical elements are Air, Earth, Water, and Fire.

- Because Atticus is immune, battling the werewolf poses injury risk but not infection risk. Dwarves make good werewolf hunters because they can't be afflicted. Humans are hiring dwarves b/c of their resistance to the virus, and Centaurs who fell into law enforcement are good at rounding up werewolves due to their superior speed and size and immunity, so it’s an interesting social dynamic of humans exploiting minorities to do their dirty work. Also, werewolves can be identified by shining a certain type of torch in their eyes, but this is not common knowledge—it’s highly specialised criminal justice knowledge, and Clara could convince Yves that Zora is a Werewolf, and Yves gives her the special torch, but she doesn’t scan as a werewolf because she never took the bite, even though she pretends that she is one.

#### *Vampire Black Plague* 

- They got it under control with vaccines, but not everyone has taken one, so people still become Vampires. Also, there are some Vampire Supremacists who wish to convert all humans to their kind. Sort of like domestic terrorists calling for the Bugaboo, they would like to see a race war.  
- It’s spread by bats instead of rats; less widespread than the Black Death due to different population dispersions of bats vs. rats.

#### *Torture and Gang Violence in London*

- A cheap and effective way to torture someone was with the use of [rats](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rat_torture). There were many variants, but the most common was to force a rat through a victim's body (usually the intestines) as a way to escape. The victim would be completely restrained and tied to the ground or a bed, and the torturer would cut slits into the victim's stomach. The torturer would then use a bowl to trap rats on the victim's stomach, then place hot coal on top of the bowl; the rats would then get hot, and after a few seconds would enter the victim's stomach. Gnawing the intestines usually resulted in a few hours of pain for the victim. This almost always resulted in death.  
- The Richardson Gang was an English crime gang based in South London, England in the 1960s. Also known as the "Torture Gang", they had a reputation as some of London's most sadistic gangsters. Their alleged specialties included pulling teeth out using pliers, cutting off toes using bolt cutters and nailing victims to floors using 6-inch nails.  
- One of London’s most effective criminal gangs was the Forty Elephants, **an all-female crime syndicate**, which operated out of Southwark in the late 19th and early 20th centuries. Although they indulged in a wide variety of criminal activities, a particular speciality of theirs was shoplifting, which they often carried out wearing coats equipped with extra large or hidden pockets and hiding places for stolen items sewn in their underclothes. 

### **Character Backstory \-** 

#### *Police Force*

##### *General Notes*

- As ships \[at the [London docks](https://www.thehistoryoflondon.co.uk/the-new-london-docks-of-the-early-19th-century/)\] waited to unload, a significant proportion of cargo was stolen by gangs that preyed on the unguarded moored vessels. Goods standing on crowded and chaotic quaysides were also at risk from criminals, sometimes in collusion with customs officers. The magistrate, social reformer and statistician Patrick Colquhoun published his Treatise on the Police of the Metropolis in 1796 in which he proposed the creation of a police force for London. He was introduced to John Harriott who, understanding the scale of criminal activity on the river, proposed a specialist force. That led to the creation of the Marine Police Establishment, based at Wapping, the forerunner of London’s Metropolitan Police.  
- Most of the police forces of the United Kingdom use a [standardised set of ranks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Police_ranks_of_the_United_Kingdom), with a slight variation in the most senior ranks for the Metropolitan Police and City of London Police. Most of the British police ranks that exist today were chosen by Home Secretary Sir Robert Peel, the founder of the Metropolitan Police, enacted under the Metropolitan Police Act 1829\. The ranks at that time were deliberately chosen so that they did not correspond with military ranking (with the exception of sergeant), because of **fears of a paramilitary force**.  
- **Frederick George Abberline** (8 January 1843 – 10 December 1929\) \- a British Chief Inspector for the London Metropolitan Police. He is best known for being a prominent police figure in the investigation into the Jack the Ripper serial killer murders of 1888\.  
- Old Bailey — The Central Criminal Court of England and Wales, commonly referred to as the Old Bailey after the street on which it stands, is a criminal court building in central London, one of several that house the Crown Court of England and Wales. The street outside follows the route of the ancient wall around the City of London, which was part of the fortification's bailey, hence the metonymic name. A Metonymic is a figure of speech in which a thing or concept is referred to by the name of something closely associated with that thing or concept, and a bailey (or ward) in a [fortification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fortification) is a courtyard enclosed by a [curtain wall](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Curtain_wall_\(fortification\)). In particular, an early type of European castle was known as a [motte-and-bailey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Motte-and-bailey). [Castles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Castle) can have more than one bailey.  
- We will have something like “The Difference Engine’s” **Bow Street Special Branch** for the Whitechapel Murders narrative arc (mostly to do with Clara, but some Atticus overlap)  
- “While some policemen managed to ascend the police hierarchy and become senior officers with high wages, position of power, prestige and a respectable standing in the community at large, thereby crossing the boundary that divided the middle from the working class, the majority of officers (between 20% and 25% at the turn of the twentieth century) never rose beyond [the rank of constable](https://www2.clarku.edu/faculty/jbrown/papers/shpayer.pdf) and had to do with low wages, hard physical work, and no supervisory status.  
- **The Flying Squad** is a group of police officers who are always ready to travel quickly to the scene of a serious crime.  
- Beadle \- (historical) a minor parish officer dealing with petty offenders.

#### *The Dockhounds*

- The Dockhounds are the most powerful crime syndicate in our version of the Victorian East End of London. They specialize in “large-scale prostitution, forgery, counterfeiting, fraud, commercial burglary and money-laundering.” Many use their belts as weapons, sharpening the tin buckles into ‘a deadly flail.’  
- Ladsman \- A criminal teaching children how to steal in exchange for a cut of profits and/or other assistance such as safe lodging.

##### *Martina, ‘Molly’ of the Hounds*

- *Molly* was ‘long a synonym for "woman of ill repute," for unknown reasons.’ She is the [moll](https://www.vocabulary.com/dictionary/moll), the mistress, the honcho of the Hounds, taking leadership after her husband was killed by a rival gang. She and Hounds avenged her husband by exterminating every last member of the rival gang, emerging from the bloody turf war victorious.  
- She has a weird half-shaved hairstyle and maybe some Eastern European-type background. Coming from a dysfunctional background, a coldness, hardness to her that she believes is 'in her blood' and can't really be unlearned, although she does have a deeply embedded soft spot, even after the tragedy of losing her love.

##### *The Ladsman*

- Carlisle McGrady, a 45 yo. deadbeat who used to be the ringleader of a band of pickpockets Atticus was involved with as a youth. He now resents Atticus for his debts to the Dockhounds, and Carlisle has a hard time recognizing Atticus if Atticus is wearing Sandhog Uniform

#### *The ‘Anglican’ [Cult](https://docs.google.com/document/u/0/d/1FACtrJausk4Gz0TfQKOXOEdBx5j07rzobqW_NvxGxr4/edit)*

- The [English Reformation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_Reformation) took place in 16th-century England when the Church of England broke away from the authority of the Pope and the Roman Catholic Church. These events were, in part, associated with the wider European Protestant Reformation, a religious and political movement that affected the practice of Christianity in western and central Europe. Causes included the invention of the printing press, increased circulation of the Bible and the transmission of new knowledge and ideas among scholars, the upper and middle classes and readers in general. The phases of the English Reformation, which also covered Wales and Ireland, were largely driven by changes in government policy, to which public opinion gradually accommodated itself.  
- Evangelicalism \- worldwide trans-denominational movement within Protestant Christianity   
- During the 19th century, the megachurches, churches with more than 2,000 people, began to develop. The first [evangelical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evangelicalism#18th_century) megachurch, the Metropolitan Tabernacle with a 6000-seat auditorium, was inaugurated in 1861 in London by Charles Spurgeon.  
- Name Ideas: "The People Risen” (from The Difference Engine)  
- Moloch \- an  idol with the head of a Bull that appears in the book of Leviticus, and seems to involve child sacrifice. "In Greek mythology, the people of Athens were at one point compelled by King Minos to choose 14 young noble citizens (seven young men and seven maidens) to be offered as sacrificial victims to the Minotaur to be killed in retribution for the death of Minos' son…” Throughout the game, the Cult is aware of Atticus and maybe helps him on certain missions/allows Atticus to live, with a plan to use Atticus and the orphans in a type of sacrificial ceremony to give the Cult leader the Power of Moloch, or, alternatively, to mechanise Atticus with enhancements, and create a Moloch-Minotaur-zombie that would be a super-soldier for the Cult. Moloch was a bull-headed deity associated with child sacrifice, which is a practice Bragg is already familiar with, having orchestrated the string of kidnappings in the East End, to fuel his experimental body-modification. In his vision of the future, Bragg hopes to mechanise Atticus with enhancements, and use the minotaur’s abilities for the interests of the Cult.

##### *The Cult Leader*

- Crippled in his youth, this Belgian (?) Cyclops inherited a boatload of money, with which he created a mechanical ventilation system to sustain his body/lungs/respiratory system, and to be able to live longer in general. During a sacrificial ceremony, he should wear a Surplice. He isn't evil so much as a victim of his upbringing and circumstance that perverted his world view.  
- Being a Cyclops gives us freedom to say that he’s capable of magic, etc.  
- The leader could be hoping to set people free from their neuroses… saying the mind is just a tool, a machine that if used properly, can evolve humanity, instead of obsessing over the impossible task of solving inner issues (a la Untethered Soul, page 95\)  
- Crossover with Clara: Clara had to flee an abusive and controlling relationship with her French husband, slowly poisoning him to death by putting a little bit of arsenic from rat poison each day into his morning tea. She then fled to Belgium (spent a few years in Brussels, learning the ropes as a con-artist, where she also met the Belgian Cult Leader coincidentally—running in the same underground circles), then to the Netherlands and finally to England to escape prosecution.  
- Potential names: Richard or **Silas Braxton Bragg**, Ryzer Hackel or Rysher or Rycher, Gustave Ruscha, **Stryver Cole**, Gustave Ryzer

#### *Clara Reed / (Corsair)*

- Previous potential names \- Lacey Virgeaux, Margeaux McCall, Margot Virgeaux, **Heyward**  
- Potential [Romantic Operas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Bohemian_Girl)/[Comic Operas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Sorcerer) \- [burlesque](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Victorian_burlesque) [ballad opera](https://www.jstor.org/stable/739642?seq=1).  
- A redeemable thief with a heart of gold… or a reluctant hero. Her potential mortality comes more from the people she's investigating—she's getting close to something or someone big, and they don't want her finding out.  
- In the Bar-chat with Atticus, the Player can say what Clara says from the opposite side of the Conversation (her POV this time) and it's like a 'Choose to Rob the Minotaur' or not sort of moment. But if we start her storyline chronologically AFTER she robs Atticus, there won't be any programming issues as far as Atticus/Clara interfacing.  
- Prison opening for her game (?) \- A treadwheel, or treadmill, is a form of engine typically powered by humans. It may resemble a water wheel in appearance, and can be worked either by a human treading paddles set into its circumference (treadmill), or by a human or animal standing inside it (treadwheel). These devices are no longer used for power or punishment, and the term "treadmill" has come to mean an exercise machine for running or walking in place.  
- She was an amateur star-gazer and dreamt of becoming an astronomer before her toxic relationship and fall from grace, so she has a little telescope set up in her tenement window that she got secondhand and repaired herself. There’s an eyewitness in her same building that in one mission she has to get to talk. She has her telescope pointed to the stars depending on the Astrological season, which she’s also into (Astrology being Astronomy’s kooky cousin). She also collects various ocular oddities such as a spyglass used by sailors and explorers, among other ocular curiosities.   
- She was in some kind of abusive/controlling relationship with her French husband, and she had to slowly poison (by putting a little bit of arsenic from rat poison each day into his morning tea). She then fled to Belgium (spent a few years in Brussels, learning the ropes as a con-artist, where she also met the Belgian Cult Leader coincidentally—running in the same underground circles), then to the Netherlands and finally to England to escape prosecution. Since then she’s assumed a new identity and has been in and out of jail, and ridden trains and gypsy caravans over from France and throughout England, Scotland and Ireland, sharpening her skills as a thief and finally a sex-worker when she settled in London, for the high-paying clientele she attracts with her well-travelled personality and wealth of intelligence and stories to tell.   
- Motivation to solve the mystery: Sympathy for the women and fear of being targeted herself; but also a detective character (a friend of the Stranger’s) approaches her early on in the game, showing her gruesome crime scene photos and case files, then offering a handsome sum for her to go undercover in hopes to catch the killer. The detective is an old police acquaintance who initially strong-arms her into it but the deeper into it she gets the more it bothers her and she gets this drive to solve the case on her own. She became an informant after her troubles with the law, so the detective (a man) kind of blackmails her or otherwise forces her hand but she realises she actually wants to help after a while. There’s also a Centaur Soldier-turned-Cop who still rocks his full regalia and has a bit of a narcissist/power-trip complex, but with a heart of gold once he reels in his ego. Seeing as there will be so much Police-work, he could even be the Precinct Manager for the 'Detective' character who convinces Clara to try and solve the case. He has a thing for Clara but she rebuffs him and manipulates him. He thinks he's a ladies man but he's full of himself, and being a little too clumsy for a soldier, he moved into police work instead.  
- Clara visits the bridge of sighs as a crime scene and converses with a spirit of a woman who committed "suicide" under mysterious circumstances. (See UTB as reference)  
- **TUNING IN** MECHANIC \- Before interactions with NPCs, Clara can start to sense the energetic auras of the other players. You get a sense immediately of the level of their anxiety, their Vigour and Nerve readings appear on the UI, and this helps with persuasion and other skill checks, as well as increases the RNG odds of winning more money from the players throughout the game. \*But should we allow the Player the option of NOT ‘tuning-in?’ My gut says that the Player should be able to argue with Clara’s own internal spirit guide (who?) but eventually is convinced, just because ‘tuning-in’ could then become something of a repeat experience throughout the game, giving her better odds at persuasion, or making it easier to make the NPC believe Clara's lies, for example.  
- She turns on a steam-pore-purifier in her dressing room as part of her evening routine.  
- Clara can interact more with the dog and cat in Sorris Square.  
- She’s at the Police Precinct, on the arm of a dandy (Tenor Cunningham) at the werewolf fights—maybe to investigate the suspect (Sykes), and at the pub with the Dockhounds.
